-- Table structure for table `messaging_tickets`
--

CREATE TABLE `messaging_tickets` (
  `id` int(11) NOT NULL,
  `user_id` int(11) NOT NULL,
  `subject` varchar(255) NOT NULL,
  `category` enum('Technical Support','Billing','Bug Report') NOT NULL,
  `status` enum('Open','Awaiting User Reply','Awaiting Admin Reply','Closed') NOT NULL DEFAULT 'Open',
  `priority` enum('Low','Medium','High') NOT NULL DEFAULT 'Medium',
  `user_seen` tinyint(1) NOT NULL DEFAULT 1,
  `admin_seen` tinyint(1) NOT NULL DEFAULT 1,
  `created_at` timestamp NOT NULL DEFAULT current_timestamp(),
  `updated_at` timestamp NOT NULL DEFAULT current_timestamp() ON UPDATE current_timestamp()
) ENGINE=InnoDB DEFAULT CHARSET=utf8mb4 COLLATE=utf8mb4_general_ci;

--
-- Table structure for table `prompt_history`
--

CREATE TABLE `prompt_history` (
  `id` int(11) NOT NULL,
  `user_id` int(11) NOT NULL,
  `prompt_type` enum('image','video','audio','lyric') NOT NULL,
  `input_mode` enum('file','text') NOT NULL DEFAULT 'file',
  `text_input` text DEFAULT NULL,
  `created_at` timestamp NOT NULL DEFAULT current_timestamp(),
  `analysis_text` text DEFAULT NULL,
  `options_text` text DEFAULT NULL,
  `branding_wall` text DEFAULT NULL,
  `branding_clothing` text DEFAULT NULL,
  `branding_background` text DEFAULT NULL,
  `output_prompt` text DEFAULT NULL,
  `output_style` text DEFAULT NULL,
  `output_theme` text DEFAULT NULL,
  `output_lyrics` text DEFAULT NULL,
  `negative_prompt` text DEFAULT NULL,
  `tags` varchar(500) DEFAULT NULL,
  `notes` text DEFAULT NULL
) ENGINE=InnoDB DEFAULT CHARSET=utf8mb4 COLLATE=utf8mb4_general_ci;

The riff is simple yet instantly recognizable, built on a distinctive, angular four-chord progression that uses a characteristic ascending motif.\n\n#### C. Grohl\'s style is often described as tight but explosive.\n*   **Sound:** Large, arena-ready drum sound. The snare is tight with significant ring. The use of the ride cymbal during the quieter verses adds a subtle, nervous undercurrent.\n\n---\n\n### IV. The song is an emotional autopsy of a broken home. **Theme:** The dissonance between the idealized image of a perfect family and the reality of deep-seated dysfunction, divorce, and the impact on the child witness. **Genre:** Pop/Rock Ballad with confessional, storytelling elements. |\n| **Overall Aesthetic Goal** | To create a visual narrative that oscillates between suffocating domestic confinement and liberating, solitary reflection. Cinematography: The Fractured View\n\n**Camera Movement & Style:**\n\n*   **Steadicam and Slow Zoom (The Mother/Father POV):** When depicting the parents, the camera movements are often slow, deliberate, and slightly detached, creating an observational, almost judgmental distance. We see the parents as the child sees them: large, immutable, and confusing figures.\n*   **Handheld and Shaky (The Child POV):** When the focus is on the protagonist (The Daughter, played by P!nk in adult form, or a younger actress), the camera is intimate, often low to the ground, reflecting a child\'s height and perspective. The handheld movement reflects her emotional instability and anxiety, especially during moments of confrontation.\n*   **Use of Shallow Depth of Field:** Focuses intensely on specific, painful details (a parent\'s clenched jaw, a forgotten toy, a stray tear), blurring the overwhelming, chaotic background.\n\n**Key Shot Types:**\n\n*   **Reflective Close-Ups:** Extreme close-ups of the protagonist\'s face reflected in mirrors, windowpanes, or even the surface of water, emphasizing isolation (\"I\'ve been a witness to your game\").\n*   **Wide, Empty Shots:** Ominous wide shots of the house interiors, showing the physical distance between family members, even when they are in the same room.\n\n### II. Color Palette and Lighting: Worn Pastels and Harsh Shadows\n\n**Color Palette:**\n\n*   **Primary Colors:** Desaturated blues (sadness, coldness), dusty rose and beige (nostalgia, faded memories), and occasional flashes of harsh, electric white (anger, revelation).\n*   **The Family Portrait:** The colors used when recreating the \"perfect\" family scenes (flashbacks) are slightly oversaturated, suggesting a forced, artificial happiness, akin to a faded photograph from the 80s or 90s.\n*   **The Present Day:** Dominated by low-key lighting, shadows, and muted, earthen tones, suggesting the protagonist is digging through old, dirty memories.\n\n**Lighting:**\n\n*   **Muted Interior Light:** Natural light struggling to pierce heavy drapes or blinds, creating strong vertical shadows (bars/imprisonment motif). The house feels perpetually dusty and dimly lit, even at midday.\n*   **Spotlight on Dysfunction:** During conflict scenes, the lighting is harsh and theatrical, often backlighting the parents to obscure their faces, turning them into silhouettes of conflict, perceived by the child.\n*   **The Yellow Glow of Nostalgia:** Brief, warm, golden light is used for the genuine, positive memory fragments (a moment of shared laughter, a birthday), making these rare glimpses feel even more precious and heartbreakingly brief.\n\n### III. Setting and Production Design: The Haunted House\n\n**The House (Main Set):**\n\n*   A large, two-story, slightly run-down suburban home that attempts to appear wealthy or respectable but is internally crumbling.\n*   **The Living Room:** The main battlefield. Overstuffed, dated furniture covered in plastic or protective slipcovers (symbolizing the emotional distance and the need to protect the *image*). A grand fireplace that is always cold.\n*   **The Hallway:** Long, dark, and filled with old photographs, culminating in a large, pristine \"Family Portrait\" hanging prominently (the central motif).\n*   **The Daughters Bedroom:** Small, safe, but cluttered with defenses (drawings, books). This is her bunker.\n\n**Key Props:**\n\n*   **The Porcelain Doll/Figurine:** A recurring motifa delicate, beautiful object that is constantly being almost knocked over or is visibly cracked, symbolizing the fragile family unit.\n*   **The Camera/Polaroid:** Used by the child/protagonist to document the moments of tension, turning the act of witnessing into a form of self-preservation.\n*   **The Frame:** Close-ups on hands polishing the glass of the large family portrait, desperately trying to wipe away the dust, only to reveal the cracks underneath.\n\n### IV. Character Actions and Emotional Arc\n\n**The Protagonist (The Daughter):**\n\n*   **Action:** Observes, hides, writes, and eventually confronts. Her body language is tense, often curled up or leaning against a wall, trying to occupy as little space as possible.\n*   **Emotion:** Anxiety, confusion, profound sadness, punctuated by moments of desperate, silent pleading for normalcy.\n*   **Design:** Dressed in simple, practical clothing (oversized shirts, faded jeans) that serves to hide her and minimize attention.\n\n**The Parents (The Mother & Father):**\n\n*   **Action:** The parents rarely touch the daughter or each other. They communicate primarily through sighs, slamming doors, or whispered, venomous arguments that the daughter strains to hear.\n*   **Design:** The parents are always dressed impeccably (even when arguing), emphasizing their commitment to maintaining the illusion of success and stability.\n\n**Scene Progression:**\n\n#### Scene 1: The Disintegration (Verses 1 & 2)\n\n*   **Visual Focus:** The house at night. Shadows are long and blue. We follow the protagonist, small and alone, navigating the silent war zone.\n*   **Action:** Flashbacks intercut with the present. The protagonist sees ghosts of arguments in the corners of rooms (quick, jarring cuts of parents yelling).\n*   **Climax:** A slow push-in on the kitchen table where one chair is now permanently empty. The Daughter silently slides a small note under the empty plate.\n\n#### Scene 2: The Confrontation and the Mirror (Chorus)\n\n*   **Visual Focus:** The bathroom mirror. The cinematographer uses the photographer\'s flash to emphasize the artificialityeach flash illuminates a brief, genuine moment of tension (a father rolling his eyes, a mother gripping the daughter\'s shoulder too tightly).\n*   **Contrast:** This scene is bright, highly saturated, and suffocatingly tight, contrasting sharply with the loose, dark cinematography of the rest of the video.\n\n#### Scene 4: Breaking the Frame (Outro)\n\n*   **Visual Focus:** The protagonist is now outside, in a neglected garden or backyard, surrounded by overgrown weeds.\n*   **Action:** She takes the large, framed family portrait out into the light.
